They sell their surplus produce, and some maintain separate fields for commercial use. Urban centres are particularly reliant on peasant agriculture for their foodstuffs. Soils and climate on the coast encourage extensive commercial cultivation of bananas, cocoa, oil palms, rubber, and tea. Inland on the South Cameroon Plateau, cash crops include coffee, sugar, and tobacco. Coffee is a major cash crop in the western highlands, and in the north, natural conditions favour crops such as cotton, groundnuts, and rice. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Taureaux_et_vaches_hollandais_%C3%A0_wallya_Cameroun.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Taureaux_et_vaches_hollandais_%C3%A0_wallya_Cameroun.jpg/220px-Taureaux_et_vaches_hollandais_%C3%A0_wallya_Cameroun.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Taureaux_et_vaches_hollandais_%C3%A0_wallya_Cameroun.jpg/330px-Taureaux_et_vaches_hollandais_%C3%A0_wallya_Cameroun.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Taureaux_et_vaches_hollandais_%C3%A0_wallya_Cameroun.jpg/440px-Taureaux_et_vaches_hollandais_%C3%A0_wallya_Cameroun.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4128" data-file-height="3096"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Taureaux_et_vaches_hollandais_%C3%A0_wallya_Cameroun.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dutch bulls and cows at Wallya community during the rainy season in Cameroon
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Livestock are raised throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Fishing employs 5,000 people and provides over 100,000 tons of seafood each year.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-awf_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awf-120">[120]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bushmeat" title="Bushmeat">Bushmeat</a>, long a staple food for rural Cameroonians, is today a delicacy in the country's urban centres. The commercial bushmeat trade has now surpassed deforestation as the main threat to wildlife in Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The southern rainforest has vast timber reserves, estimated to cover 37% of Cameroon's total land area.<sup id="cite_ref-awf_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awf-120">[120]</a></sup> However, large areas of the forest are difficult to reach. Logging, largely handled by foreign-owned firms,<sup id="cite_ref-awf_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-awf-120">[120]</a></sup> provides the government US$60&nbsp;million a year in taxes (as of 1998<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>), and laws mandate the safe and sustainable exploitation of timber. Nevertheless, in practice, the industry is one of the least regulated in Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Factory-based industry accounted for an estimated 26.5% of GDP in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> More than 75% of Cameroon's industrial strength is located in <a href="/wiki/Douala" title="Douala">Douala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bonab%C3%A9ri" title="Bonabéri">Bonabéri</a>. Cameroon possesses substantial mineral resources, but these are not extensively mined (see <i><a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Cameroon" class="mw-redirect" title="Mining in Cameroon">Mining in Cameroon</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-State_Dept_49-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-State_Dept-49">[49]</a></sup> Petroleum exploitation has fallen since 1986, but this is still a substantial sector such that dips in prices have a strong effect on the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Rapids and waterfalls obstruct the southern rivers, but these sites offer opportunities for hydroelectric development and supply most of Cameroon's energy. The Sanaga River powers the largest hydroelectric station, located at Edéa. The rest of Cameroon's energy comes from oil-powered thermal engines. Much of the country remains without reliable power supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Cameroon" title="Transport in Cameroon">Transport in Cameroon</a> is often difficult. Only 6.6% of the roadways are tarred.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> Roadblocks often serve little other purpose than to allow police and gendarmes to collect bribes from travellers.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> Road banditry has long hampered transport along the eastern and western borders, and since 2005, the problem has intensified in the east as the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> has further destabilised.<sup id="cite_ref-Musa_Gunmen_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Musa_Gunmen-127">[127]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bateau_au_port_de_Douala1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bateau_au_port_de_Douala1.jpg/220px-Bateau_au_port_de_Douala1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bateau_au_port_de_Douala1.jpg/330px-Bateau_au_port_de_Douala1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bateau_au_port_de_Douala1.jpg/440px-Bateau_au_port_de_Douala1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bateau_au_port_de_Douala1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Douala seaport
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Intercity_bus_service" title="Intercity bus service">Intercity bus services</a> run by multiple private companies connect all major cities. They are the most popular means of transportation followed by the rail service <i><a href="/wiki/Camrail" title="Camrail">Camrail</a></i>. Rail service runs from <a href="/wiki/Kumba" title="Kumba">Kumba</a> in the west to <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9labo" title="Bélabo">Bélabo</a> in the east and north to <a href="/wiki/Ngaound%C3%A9r%C3%A9" title="Ngaoundéré">Ngaoundéré</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> International airports are located in <a href="/wiki/Douala_International_Airport" title="Douala International Airport">Douala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9_Nsimalen_International_Airport" title="Yaoundé Nsimalen International Airport">Yaoundé</a>, with a third under construction in <a href="/wiki/Maroua" title="Maroua">Maroua</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Douala is the country's principal seaport.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> In the north, the Bénoué River is seasonally navigable from Garoua across into Nigeria.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although press freedoms have improved since the first decade of the 21st century, the press is corrupt and beholden to special interests and political groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Reporters_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reporters-132">[132]</a></sup> Newspapers routinely self-censor to avoid government reprisals.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_71-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-71">[71]</a></sup> The major radio and television stations are state-run and other <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Cameroon" class="mw-redirect" title="Communications in Cameroon">communications</a>, such as land-based telephones and telegraphs, are largely under government control.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> However, cell phone networks and Internet providers have increased dramatically since the first decade of the 21st century<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> and are largely unregulated.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Armed_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Cameroonian Armed Forces">Cameroonian Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vehicules_militaires_pendant_le_d%C3%A9fil%C3%A97.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Vehicules_militaires_pendant_le_d%C3%A9fil%C3%A97.jpg/220px-Vehicules_militaires_pendant_le_d%C3%A9fil%C3%A97.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Vehicules_militaires_pendant_le_d%C3%A9fil%C3%A97.jpg/330px-Vehicules_militaires_pendant_le_d%C3%A9fil%C3%A97.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Vehicules_militaires_pendant_le_d%C3%A9fil%C3%A97.jpg/440px-Vehicules_militaires_pendant_le_d%C3%A9fil%C3%A97.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vehicules_militaires_pendant_le_d%C3%A9fil%C3%A97.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Military vehicles during a parade.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Cameroon Armed Forces, (French: <i>Forces armées camerounaises</i>, FAC) as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, consists of the country's army (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i>Armée de Terre</i>), the country's navy (French: <i>Marine Nationale de la République</i> (MNR), includes naval infantry), the Cameroonian Air Force (French: <i>Armée de l'Air du Cameroun</i>, AAC), and the <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">Gendarmerie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Males and females that are 18 years of age up to 23 years of age and have graduated high school are eligible for military service. Those who join are obliged to complete 4 years of service. There is no conscription in Cameroon, but the government makes periodic calls for volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Cameroon" title="Demographics of Cameroon">Demographics of Cameroon</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The population of Cameroon was 25,216,267 in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-136">[136]</a></sup> The life expectancy was 62.3&nbsp;years (60.6&nbsp;years for males and 64&nbsp;years for females).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GedWomenDay.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/GedWomenDay.JPG/220px-GedWomenDay.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/GedWomenDay.JPG/330px-GedWomenDay.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/GedWomenDay.JPG/440px-GedWomenDay.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GedWomenDay.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cameroonian women on Women's Day Celebration
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Cameroon has slightly more women (50.5%) than men (49.5%). Over 60% of the population is under age 25. People over 65 years of age account for only 3.11% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Cameroon's population is almost evenly divided between urban and rural dwellers.<sup id="cite_ref-West_3_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_3-137">[137]</a></sup> Population density is highest in the large urban centres, the western highlands, and the northeastern plain.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Douala, Yaoundé, and <a href="/wiki/Garoua" title="Garoua">Garoua</a> are the largest cities. In contrast, the Adamawa Plateau, southeastern Bénoué depression, and most of the South Cameroon Plateau are sparsely populated.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> was 4.8 in 2013 with a population growth rate of 2.56%.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>People from the overpopulated western highlands and the underdeveloped north are moving to the coastal plantation zone and urban centres for employment.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Smaller movements are occurring as workers seek employment in lumber mills and plantations in the south and east.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> Although the national sex ratio is relatively even, these out-migrants are primarily males, which leads to unbalanced ratios in some regions.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maison_obus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Maison_obus.jpg/220px-Maison_obus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Maison_obus.jpg/330px-Maison_obus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Maison_obus.jpg/440px-Maison_obus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1060" data-file-height="688"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maison_obus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The homes of the <a href="/wiki/Musgum_dwelling_units" class="mw-redirect" title="Musgum dwelling units">Musgum</a>, in the Far North Region, are made of earth and grass.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Both <a href="/wiki/Monogamy" title="Monogamy">monogamous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polygamy" title="Polygamy">polygamous</a> marriage are practised, and the average Cameroonian family is large and extended.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> In the north, women tend to the home, and men herd cattle or work as farmers. In the south, women grow the family's food, and men provide meat and grow cash crops. Cameroonian society is male-dominated, and violence and discrimination against women is common.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedom_House_59-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_House-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_71-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The number of distinct ethnic and linguistic groups in Cameroon is estimated to be between 230 and 282.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The Adamawa Plateau broadly bisects these into northern and southern divisions. The northern peoples are Sudanese groups, who live in the central highlands and the northern lowlands, and the Fulani, who are spread throughout northern Cameroon. A small number of <a href="/wiki/Baggara" title="Baggara">Shuwa</a> Arabs live near Lake Chad. Southern Cameroon is inhabited by speakers of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-Bantu" title="Semi-Bantu">Semi-Bantu</a> languages. Bantu-speaking groups inhabit the coastal and equatorial zones, while speakers of Semi-Bantu languages live in the Western grassfields. Some 5,000 Gyele and Baka <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_peoples" title="Pygmy peoples">Pygmy peoples</a> roam the southeastern and coastal rainforests or live in small, roadside settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Nigerians make up the largest group of foreign nationals.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><br> </p>

        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">3</td>

        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">4</td> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Bamenda" title="Bamenda">Bamenda</a></td>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Refugees">Refugees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Refugees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Refugees_in_Cameroon" title="Refugees in Cameroon">Refugees in Cameroon</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2007, Cameroon hosted approximately 97,400 refugees and asylum seekers. Of these, 49,300 were from the Central African Republic (many driven west by war),<sup id="cite_ref-RCross_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RCross-150">[150]</a></sup> 41,600 from <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>, and 2,900 from <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-151">[151]</a></sup> Kidnappings of Cameroonian citizens by Central African bandits have increased since 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-Musa_Gunmen_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Musa_Gunmen-127">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the first months of 2014, thousands of refugees fleeing the violence in the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> arrived in Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 4 June 2014, AlertNet reported: </p> 
      <blockquote> 
       <p>Almost 90,000 people have fled to neighbouring Cameroon since December and up to 2,000 a week, mostly women and children, are still crossing the border, the United Nations said. </p>
       <p>"Women and children are arriving in Cameroon in a shocking state, after weeks, sometimes months, on the road, foraging for food," said Ertharin Cousin, executive director of the <a href="/wiki/World_Food_Programme" title="World Food Programme">World Food Programme</a> (WFP).<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> </p> 
      </blockquote> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Cameroon" title="Languages of Cameroon">Languages of Cameroon</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Both English and French are official languages, although French is by far the most understood language (more than 80%).<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> German, the language of the original colonisers, has long since been displaced by French and English. <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_Pidgin_English" title="Cameroonian Pidgin English">Cameroonian Pidgin English</a> is the lingua franca in the formerly British-administered territories.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> A mixture of English, French, and Pidgin called <a href="/wiki/Camfranglais" title="Camfranglais">Camfranglais</a> has been gaining popularity in urban centres since the mid-1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Niba_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Niba-157">[157]</a></sup> The government encourages bilingualism in English and French, and as such, official government documents, new legislation, ballots, among others, are written and provided in both languages. As part of the initiative to encourage bilingualism in Cameroon, six of the eight universities in the country are entirely bilingual. </p>
      <p>In addition to the colonial languages, there are approximately 250 other languages spoken by nearly 20&nbsp;million Cameroonians.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-8">[8]</a></sup> It is because of this that Cameroon is considered one of the most linguistically diverse countries in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-7">[7]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the northern regions of the <a href="/wiki/Far_North_Region,_Cameroon" title="Far North Region, Cameroon">Far North Region, Cameroon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/North_Region,_Cameroon" class="mw-redirect" title="North Region, Cameroon">North Region, Cameroon</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Adamawa_Region" title="Adamawa Region">Adamawa Region</a>, the Fulani language <a href="/wiki/Fulfulde" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulfulde">Fulfulde</a> is the lingua franca with French merely serving as an administrative language. However, <a href="/wiki/Chadian_Arabic" title="Chadian Arabic">Chadian Arabic</a> in the Far North's Region's department of <a href="/wiki/Logone-et-Chari" title="Logone-et-Chari">Logone-et-Chari</a> acts as the lingua franca irrespective of ethnic groups. </p>
      <p>In 2017 there were language protests by the anglophone population against perceived oppression by the francophone.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-158">[158]</a></sup> The military was deployed against the protesters and people had been killed, hundreds imprisoned and thousands fled the country.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> This culminated in the declaration of an independent <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ambazonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Ambazonia">Republic of Ambazonia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> which has since evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Anglophone_Crisis" title="Anglophone Crisis">Anglophone Crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-158">[158]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cameroon" title="Religion in Cameroon">Religion in Cameroon</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5"><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cameroon" title="Religion in Cameroon">Religion in Cameroon</a> (2018 estimate by <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_1-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-1">[1]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td>

          </tr> 
          <tr>

            <div style="background:yellow; width:38.3%; overflow: hidden;">

          </tr>

            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">25.5%</td> 
          </tr>

            <div style="background:red; width:2.2%; overflow: hidden;">

          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">Other, including other Christian</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:gray; width:8.1%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td>

          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>Cameroon has a high level of <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cameroon" title="Religion in Cameroon">religious freedom</a> and diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_71-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-71">[71]</a></sup> The predominant faith is <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, practised by about two-thirds of the population, while <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is a significant minority faith, adhered to by about one-fourth. In addition, traditional faiths are practised by many. Muslims are most concentrated in the north, while Christians are concentrated primarily in the southern and western regions, but practitioners of both faiths can be found throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-161">[161]</a></sup> Large cities have significant populations of both groups.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-161">[161]</a></sup> Muslims in Cameroon are divided into <a href="/wiki/Sufis" class="mw-redirect" title="Sufis">Sufis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salafi" class="mw-redirect" title="Salafi">Salafis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Economist_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-162">[162]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shias</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-denominational Muslims">non-denominational Muslims</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Economist_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Economist-162">[162]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>People from the North-West and South-West provinces, which used to be a part of <a href="/wiki/British_Cameroons" class="mw-redirect" title="British Cameroons">British Cameroons</a>, have the highest proportion of Protestants. The French-speaking regions of the southern and western regions are largely Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_161-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-161">[161]</a></sup> Southern ethnic groups predominantly follow Christian or traditional African <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animist</a> beliefs, or a <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretic</a> combination of the two. People widely believe in witchcraft, and the government outlaws such practices.<sup id="cite_ref-Geschiere_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geschiere-164">[164]</a></sup> Suspected witches are often subject to mob violence.<sup id="cite_ref-Human_Rights_Report_71-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_Rights_Report-71">[71]</a></sup> The Islamist jihadist group <a href="/wiki/Ansar_al-Islam" title="Ansar al-Islam">Ansar al-Islam</a> has been reported as operating in North Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the northern regions, the locally dominant <a href="/wiki/Fulani" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulani">Fulani</a> ethnic group is mostly Muslim, but the overall population is fairly evenly divided among Muslims, Christians, and followers of indigenous religious beliefs (called <i><a href="/wiki/Kirdi" title="Kirdi">Kirdi</a></i> ("pagan") by the Fulani).<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_161-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-161">[161]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bamum_people" title="Bamum people">Bamum</a> ethnic group of the West Region is largely Muslim.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_161-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-161">[161]</a></sup> Native traditional religions are practised in rural areas throughout the country but rarely are practised publicly in cities, in part because many indigenous religious groups are intrinsically local in character.<sup id="cite_ref-IRFR_161-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRFR-161">[161]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Cameroon" title="Culture of Cameroon">Culture of Cameroon</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Music and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Cameroon" title="Public holidays in Cameroon">Public holidays in Cameroon</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg/170px-Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg/255px-Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/54/Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="313" data-file-height="336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Baka_dancers_June_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Dancers greet visitors to the East Region.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Cameroon" title="Music of Cameroon">Music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance_in_Cameroon" title="Dance in Cameroon">dance</a> are an integral part of Cameroonian ceremonies, festivals, social gatherings, and storytelling.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-West_18_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_18-167">[167]</a></sup> Traditional dances are highly choreographed and separate men and women or forbid participation by one sex altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> The goals of dances range from pure entertainment to religious devotion.<sup id="cite_ref-West_18_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_18-167">[167]</a></sup> Traditionally, music is transmitted orally. In a typical performance, a chorus of singers echoes a soloist.<sup id="cite_ref-Mbaku_189_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_189-169">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Musical accompaniment may be as simple as clapping hands and stomping feet,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> but traditional instruments include bells worn by dancers, clappers, drums and <a href="/wiki/Talking_drum" title="Talking drum">talking drums</a>, flutes, horns, rattles, scrapers, stringed instruments, whistles, and xylophones; the exact combination varies with ethnic group and region. Some performers sing complete songs by themselves, accompanied by a harplike instrument.<sup id="cite_ref-Mbaku_189_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_189-169">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Popular music styles include <a href="/wiki/Ambasse_bey" title="Ambasse bey">ambasse bey</a> of the coast, <a href="/wiki/Assiko" title="Assiko">assiko</a> of the Bassa, <a href="/wiki/Mangambeu" title="Mangambeu">mangambeu</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bamileke" class="mw-redirect" title="Bamileke">Bangangte</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tsamassi" title="Tsamassi">tsamassi</a> of the Bamileke.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Nigeria" title="Music of Nigeria">Nigerian music</a> has influenced Anglophone Cameroonian performers, and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Nico_Mbarga" title="Prince Nico Mbarga">Prince Nico Mbarga</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Highlife" title="Highlife">highlife</a> hit "<a href="/wiki/Sweet_Mother" title="Sweet Mother">Sweet Mother</a>" is the top-selling African record in history.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The two most popular styles of music are <a href="/wiki/Makossa" title="Makossa">makossa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bikutsi" title="Bikutsi">bikutsi</a>. Makossa developed in Douala and mixes folk music, highlife, <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">Congo music</a>. Performers such as <a href="/wiki/Manu_Dibango" title="Manu Dibango">Manu Dibango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_Bebey" title="Francis Bebey">Francis Bebey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moni_Bil%C3%A9" title="Moni Bilé">Moni Bilé</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Petit-Pays" title="Petit-Pays">Petit-Pays</a> popularised the style worldwide in the 1970s and 1980s. Bikutsi originated as war music among the Ewondo. Artists such as <a href="/wiki/Anne-Marie_Nzi%C3%A9" title="Anne-Marie Nzié">Anne-Marie Nzié</a> developed it into a popular dance music beginning in the 1940s, and performers such as <a href="/wiki/Mama_Ohandja" title="Mama Ohandja">Mama Ohandja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Les_T%C3%AAtes_Brul%C3%A9es" title="Les Têtes Brulées">Les Têtes Brulées</a> popularised it internationally during the 1960s, 1970s, and 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nkolo_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nkolo-175">[175]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays">Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Cameroon" title="Public holidays in Cameroon">Public holidays in Cameroon</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The most notable holiday associated with patriotism in Cameroon is <a href="/wiki/National_Day_(Cameroon)" title="National Day (Cameroon)">National Day</a>, also called Unity Day. Among the most notable religious holidays are <a href="/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary" title="Assumption of Mary">Assumption Day</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ascension_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Ascension Day">Ascension Day</a> which typically occurs 39 days after Easter. In the North West and South West provinces, collectively called <a href="/wiki/Ambazonia" title="Ambazonia">Ambazonia</a>, the 1st of October is considered to be a national holiday by <a href="/wiki/Ambazonian" class="mw-redirect" title="Ambazonian">Ambazonians</a>, a date which Ambazonians regard as the declaration of independence of <a href="/wiki/Ambazonia" title="Ambazonia">Ambazonia</a> from Cameroon.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cameroonian_cuisine" title="Cameroonian cuisine">Cameroonian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ndol%C3%A8_%C3%A0_la_viande_,_morrue_et_crevette.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Ndol%C3%A8_%C3%A0_la_viande_%2C_morrue_et_crevette.jpg/220px-Ndol%C3%A8_%C3%A0_la_viande_%2C_morrue_et_crevette.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Ndol%C3%A8_%C3%A0_la_viande_%2C_morrue_et_crevette.jpg/330px-Ndol%C3%A8_%C3%A0_la_viande_%2C_morrue_et_crevette.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Ndol%C3%A8_%C3%A0_la_viande_%2C_morrue_et_crevette.jpg/440px-Ndol%C3%A8_%C3%A0_la_viande_%2C_morrue_et_crevette.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="723"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ndol%C3%A8_%C3%A0_la_viande_,_morrue_et_crevette.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Plantains and "Bobolo" served with Ndolè (meat, and shrimp). Bobolo is made from cassava
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Cameroon" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Cameroon">Cuisine</a> varies by region, but a large, one-course, evening meal is common throughout the country. A typical dish is based on cocoyams, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a> (manioc), <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Yam_(vegetable)" title="Yam (vegetable)">yams</a>, often pounded into dough-like <a href="/wiki/Fufu" title="Fufu">fufu</a>. This is served with a sauce, soup, or stew made from greens, <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">groundnuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palm_oil" title="Palm oil">palm oil</a>, or other ingredients.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> Meat and fish are popular but expensive additions, with chicken often reserved for special occasions.<sup id="cite_ref-Mbaku_121-2_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mbaku_121-2-178">[178]</a></sup> Dishes are often quite hot, spiced with salt, red pepper sauce, and <a href="/wiki/Maggi" title="Maggi">Maggi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Cutlery is common, but food is traditionally manipulated with the right hand. Breakfast consists of leftovers of bread and fruit with <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">tea</a>. Generally breakfast is made from wheat flour in various different foods such as puff-puff (doughnuts), accra banana made from <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a> and flour, bean cakes and many more. Snacks are popular, especially in larger towns where they may be bought from <a href="/wiki/Street_vendor" class="mw-redirect" title="Street vendor">street vendors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Water, <a href="/wiki/Palm_wine" title="Palm wine">palm wine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Millet_beer" title="Millet beer">millet beer</a> are the traditional mealtime drinks, although beer, soda, and wine have gained popularity. 33 Export beer is the official drink of the <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">national soccer team</a> and one of the most popular brands, joining Castel, <a href="/wiki/Amstel_Brewery" title="Amstel Brewery">Amstel Brewery</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guinness_Foreign_Extra_Stout" title="Guinness Foreign Extra Stout">Guinness</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fashion">Fashion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Fashion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Camerounais_en_tenue_traditionnelle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Camerounais_en_tenue_traditionnelle.jpg/170px-Camerounais_en_tenue_traditionnelle.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Camerounais_en_tenue_traditionnelle.jpg/255px-Camerounais_en_tenue_traditionnelle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Camerounais_en_tenue_traditionnelle.jpg/340px-Camerounais_en_tenue_traditionnelle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="4608"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Camerounais_en_tenue_traditionnelle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Cameroonian fashion is varied and often mixes modern and traditional elements. Note the wearing of <a href="/wiki/Sun_glasses" class="mw-redirect" title="Sun glasses">sun glasses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monk_shoe" title="Monk shoe">Monk shoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandals" class="mw-redirect" title="Sandals">sandals</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Smartwatch" title="Smartwatch">Smartwatch</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Cameroon's relatively large and diverse population is also diverse with respect to its contemporary fashion. Climate, religious, ethnic and cultural belief systems as well as influences from colonialism, imperialism and globalization are all reflected in the clothes worn by modern Cameroonians. </p>
      <p>Notable Cameroonian articles of clothing include: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pagnes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pagnes (page does not exist)">Pagnes</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Sarong" title="Sarong">sarongs</a> worn by Cameroon women; <a href="/wiki/Chechia" class="mw-redirect" title="Chechia">Chechia</a>, a traditional hat; kwa, a male handbag; and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandura&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gandura (page does not exist)">Gandura</a>, male custom attire.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Wrappers and <a href="/wiki/Loincloths" class="mw-redirect" title="Loincloths">loincloths</a> are used extensively by both women and men but their use varies by region with influences from <a href="/wiki/Fulani" class="mw-redirect" title="Fulani">Fulani</a> styles more present in the north and <a href="/wiki/Igbo_people" title="Igbo people">Igbo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">Yoruba</a> styles found more often in the south and west.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Imane_Ayissi" title="Imane Ayissi">Imane Ayissi</a> is one of Cameroon's top fashion designers and has received international recognition.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_arts_and_crafts">Local arts and crafts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Local arts and crafts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg/220px-Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg/330px-Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg/440px-Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1485" data-file-height="1173"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Woman_weaving_baskets_near_Lake_Ossa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A woman weaves a basket near <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ossa" title="Lake Ossa">Lake Ossa</a>, Littoral Region. Cameroonians practise such handicrafts throughout the country.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditional arts and crafts are practiced throughout the country for commercial, decorative, and religious purposes. Woodcarvings and sculptures are especially common.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> The high-quality clay of the western highlands is suitable for pottery and ceramics.<sup id="cite_ref-West_18_167-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_18-167">[167]</a></sup> Other crafts include <a href="/wiki/Basket_weaving" title="Basket weaving">basket weaving</a>, beadworking, brass and bronze working, calabash carving and painting, embroidery, and leather working. Traditional housing styles make use of locally available materials and vary from temporary wood-and-leaf shelters of nomadic <a href="/wiki/Wodaabe" title="Wodaabe">Mbororo</a> to the rectangular mud-and-thatch homes of southern peoples. Dwellings made from materials such as cement and tin are increasingly common.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">Contemporary art</a> is mainly promoted by independent cultural organizations (<a href="/wiki/Doual%27art" title="Doual'art">Doual'art</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Africr%C3%A9a&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Africréa (page does not exist)">Africréa</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Artist-run_initiative" title="Artist-run initiative">artist-run initiatives</a> (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Art_Wash&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Art Wash (page does not exist)">Art Wash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atelier_Viking" title="Atelier Viking">Atelier Viking</a>, <a href="/wiki/ArtBakery" title="ArtBakery">ArtBakery</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Cameroon" title="Literature of Cameroon">Literature of Cameroon</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Cameroonian literature has concentrated on both European and African themes. Colonial-era writers such as <a href="/wiki/Louis-Marie_Pouka" title="Louis-Marie Pouka">Louis-Marie Pouka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sankie_Maimo" title="Sankie Maimo">Sankie Maimo</a> were educated by European missionary societies and advocated <a href="/wiki/Cultural_assimilation" title="Cultural assimilation">assimilation</a> into European culture as the means to bring Cameroon into the modern world.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, writers such as <a href="/wiki/Mongo_Beti" title="Mongo Beti">Mongo Beti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Oyono" title="Ferdinand Oyono">Ferdinand Oyono</a> analysed and criticised colonialism and rejected assimilation.<sup id="cite_ref-Fitzpatrick_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fitzpatrick-191">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Volet_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Volet-193">[193]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Films_and_literature">Films and literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Films and literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Cameroon" title="Cinema of Cameroon">Cinema of Cameroon</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Shortly after independence, filmmakers such as <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Ngassa" title="Jean-Paul Ngassa">Jean-Paul Ngassa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9r%C3%A8se_Sita-Bella" title="Thérèse Sita-Bella">Thérèse Sita-Bella</a> explored similar themes.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> In the 1960s, <a href="/wiki/Mongo_Beti" title="Mongo Beti">Mongo Beti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_L%C3%A9opold_Oyono" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferdinand Léopold Oyono">Ferdinand Léopold Oyono</a> and other writers explored post-colonialism, problems of African development, and the recovery of African identity.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> Meanwhile, in the mid-1970s, filmmakers such as <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Dikongu%C3%A9_Pipa" title="Jean-Pierre Dikongué Pipa">Jean-Pierre Dikongué Pipa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Kamwa" title="Daniel Kamwa">Daniel Kamwa</a> dealt with the conflicts between traditional and post-colonial society. Literature and films during the next two decades concentrated more on wholly Cameroonian themes.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Cameroon" title="Sport in Cameroon">Sport in Cameroon</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg/220px-Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg/330px-Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg/440px-Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="731" data-file-height="581"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cameroon_vs_Germany_2003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a> faces <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> at <a href="/wiki/Zentralstadion" class="mw-redirect" title="Zentralstadion">Zentralstadion</a> in Leipzig, 17 November 2004.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>National policy strongly advocates sport in all forms. Traditional sports include canoe racing and wrestling, and several hundred runners participate in the 40&nbsp;km (25&nbsp;mi) <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon_Race_of_Hope" title="Mount Cameroon Race of Hope">Mount Cameroon Race of Hope</a> each year.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> Cameroon is one of the few tropical countries to have <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_at_the_2002_Winter_Olympics" title="Cameroon at the 2002 Winter Olympics">competed</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympic_Games" title="Winter Olympic Games">Winter Olympics</a>. </p>
      <p>Sport in Cameroon is dominated by football. Amateur football clubs abound, organised along ethnic lines or under corporate sponsors. The <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">national team</a> has been one of the most successful in Africa since its strong showing in the <a href="/wiki/1982_Football_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="1982 Football World Cup">1982</a> and <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990 FIFA World Cups</a>. Cameroon has won five <a href="/wiki/African_Cup_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="African Cup of Nations">African Cup of Nations</a> titles and the gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2000_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2000 Summer Olympics – Men's tournament">2000 Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Cameroon was the host country of the <a href="/wiki/Africa_Women_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Women Cup of Nations">Women Africa Cup of Nations</a> in November–December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Cameroon women's national football team">women's football team</a> is known as the "Indomitable Lionesses." </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>
      <div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright"> 
       <ul> 
        <li><span><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Cameroon.svg/32px-Flag_of_Cameroon.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="21" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Cameroon.svg/48px-Flag_of_Cameroon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Flag_of_Cameroon.svg/64px-Flag_of_Cameroon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Cameroon" title="Portal:Cameroon">Cameroon portal</a></span></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cameroon&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-CIA-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-CIA_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-CIA_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a          <li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.etymonline.com/word/cameroon">Cameroon (adj.)</a> nation in West Africa, its name is taken from the Anglicized form of the former name of the River Wouri, which was called by the Portuguese Rio dos Camarões "river of prawns" (16c.) for the abundance of these they found in its broad estuary. camarões is from Latin cammarus "a crawfish, prawn."</span> </li>
